Read complete contents of a file\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Reads complete file contents with UTF-8 encoding\n\n- **read_multiple_files**\n  - Read multiple files simultaneously\n  - Input: `paths` (string[])\n  - Failed reads won't stop the entire operation\n\n- **write_file**\n  - Create new file or overwrite existing (exercise caution with this)\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): File location\n    - `content` (string): File content\n\n- **edit_file**\n  - Make selective edits using advanced pattern matching and formatting\n  - Features:\n    - Line-based and multi-line content matching\n    - Whitespace normalization with indentation preservation\n    - Multiple simultaneous edits with correct positioning\n    - Indentation style detection and preservation\n    - Git-style diff output with context\n    - Preview changes with dry run mode\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): File to edit\n    - `edits` (array): List of edit operations\n      - `oldText` (string): Text to search for (can be substring)\n      - `newText` (string): Text to replace with\n    - `dryRun` (boolean): Preview changes without applying (default: false)\n  - Returns detailed diff and match information for dry runs, otherwise applies changes\n  - Best Practice: Always use dryRun first to preview changes before applying them\n\n- **create_directory**\n  - Create new directory or ensure it exists\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Creates parent directories if needed\n  - Succeeds silently if directory exists\n\n- **list_directory**\n  - List directory contents with [FILE] or [DIR] prefixes\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n\n- **move_file**\n  - Move or rename files and directories\n  - Inputs:\n    - `source` (string)\n    - `destination` (string)\n  - Fails if destination exists\n\n- **search_files**\n  - Recursively search for files/directories\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): Starting directory\n    - `pattern` (string): Search pattern\n    - `excludePatterns` (string[]): Exclude any patterns. Glob formats are supported.\n  - Case-insensitive matching\n  - Returns full paths to matches\n\n- **get_file_info**\n  - Get detailed file/directory metadata\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Returns:\n    - Size\n    - Creation time\n    - Modified time\n    - Access time\n    - Type (file/directory)\n    - Permissions\n\n- **list_allowed_directories**\n  - List all directories the server is allowed to access\n  - No input required\n  - Returns:\n    - Directories that this server can read/write from\n\n## Usage with Claude Desktop\nAdd this to your `claude_desktop_config.json`:\n\nNote: you can provide sandboxed directories to the server by mounting them to `/projects`. Adding the `ro` flag will make the directory readonly by the server.\n\n### Docker\nNote: all directories must be mounted to `/projects` by default.\n\n```json\n{\n  \"mcpServers\": {\n    \"filesystem\": {\n      \"command\": \"docker\",\n      \"args\": [\n        \"run\",\n        \"-i\",\n        \"--rm\",\n        \"--mount\", First, I'll load the MCP documentation to understand how to properly set up an MCP server.\n\n<load_mcp_documentation>\n</load_mcp_documentation>"}]},{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"[load_mcp_documentation] Result:"},{"type":"text","text":"## Creating an MCP Server\n\nWhen creating MCP servers, it's important to understand that they operate in a non-interactive environment. The server cannot initiate OAuth flows, open browser windows, or prompt for user input during runtime. All credentials and authentication tokens must be provided upfront through environment variables in the MCP settings configuration. For example, Spotify's API uses OAuth to get a refresh token for the user, but the MCP server cannot initiate this flow. While you can walk the user through obtaining an application client ID and secret, you may have to create a separate one-time setup script (like get-refresh-token.js) that captures and logs the final piece of the puzzle: the user's refresh token (i.e. you might run the script using execute_command which would open a browser for authentication, and then log the refresh token so that you can see it in the command output for you to use in the MCP settings configuration).\n\nUnless the user specifies otherwise, new MCP servers should be created in: C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\n\n### Example MCP Server\n\nFor example, if the user wanted to give you the ability to retrieve weather information, you could create an MCP server that uses the OpenWeather API to get weather information, add it to the MCP settings configuration file, and then notice that you now have access to new tools and resources in the system prompt that you might use to show the user your new capabilities.\n\nThe following example demonstrates how to build an MCP server that provides weather data functionality. While this example shows how to implement resources, resource templates, and tools, in practice you should prefer using tools since they are more flexible and can handle dynamic parameters. The resource and resource template implementations are included here mainly for demonstration purposes of the different MCP capabilities, but a real weather server would likely just expose tools for fetching weather data. (The following steps are for macOS)\n\n1. Use the `create-typescript-server` tool to bootstrap a new project in the default MCP servers directory:\n\n```bash\ncd C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\nnpx @modelcontextprotocol/create-server weather-server\ncd weather-server\n# Install dependencies\nnpm install axios\n```\n\nThis will create a new project with the following structure:\n\n```\nweather-server/\n  ├── package.json\n      {\n        ...\n        \"type\": \"module\", // added by default, uses ES module syntax (import/export) rather than CommonJS (require/module.exports) (Important to know if you create additional scripts in this server repository like a get-refresh-token.js script)\n        \"scripts\": {\n          \"build\": \"tsc && node -e \"require('fs').chmodSync('build/index.js', '755')\"\",\n          ...\n        }\n        ...\n      }\n  ├── tsconfig.json\n  └── src/\n      └── weather-server/\n          └── index.ts      # Main server implementation\n```\n\n2. Replace `src/index.ts` with the following:\n\n```typescript\n#!/usr/bin/env node\nimport { Server } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/index.js';\nimport { StdioServerTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/stdio.js';\nimport {\n  CallToolRequestSchema,\n  ErrorCode,\n  ListResourcesRequestSchema,\n  ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n  ListToolsRequestSchema,\n  McpError,\n  ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n} from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/types.js';\nimport axios from 'axios';\n\nconst API_KEY = process.env.OPENWEATHER_API_KEY; // provided by MCP config\nif (!API_KEY) {\n  throw new Error('OPENWEATHER_API_KEY environment variable is required');\n}\n\ninterface OpenWeatherResponse {\n  main: {\n    temp: number;\n    humidity: number;\n  };\n  weather: [{ description: string }];\n  wind: { speed: number };\n  dt_txt?: string;\n}\n\nconst isValidForecastArgs = (\n  args: any\n): args is { city: string; days?: number } =>\n  typeof args === 'object' &&\n  args !== null &&\n  typeof args.city === 'string' &&\n  (args.days === undefined || typeof args.days === 'number');\n\nclass WeatherServer {\n  private server: Server;\n  private axiosInstance;\n\n  constructor() {\n    this.server = new Server(\n      {\n        name: 'example-weather-server',\n        version: '0.1.0',\n      },\n      {\n        capabilities: {\n          resources: {},\n          tools: {},\n        },\n      }\n    );\n\n    this.axiosInstance = axios.create({\n      baseURL: 'http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5',\n      params: {\n        appid: API_KEY,\n        units: 'metric',\n      },\n    });\n\n    this.setupResourceHandlers();\n    this.setupToolHandlers();\n    \n    // Error handling\n    this.server.onerror = (error) => console.error('[MCP Error]', error);\n    process.on('SIGINT', async () => {\n      await this.server.close();\n      process.exit(0);\n    });\n  }\n\n  // MCP Resources represent any kind of UTF-8 encoded data that an MCP server wants to make available to clients, such as database records, API responses, log files, and more. Servers define direct resources with a static URI or dynamic resources with a URI template that follows the format `[protocol]://[host]/[path]`.\n  private setupResourceHandlers() {\n    // For static resources, servers can expose a list of resources:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListResourcesRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      resources: [\n        // This is a poor example since you could use the resource template to get the same information but this demonstrates how to define a static resource\n        {\n          uri: `weather://San Francisco/current`, // Unique identifier for San Francisco weather resource\n          name: `Current weather in San Francisco`, // Human-readable name\n          mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n          // Optional description\n          description:\n            'Real-time weather data for San Francisco including temperature, conditions, humidity, and wind speed',\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    // For dynamic resources, servers can expose resource templates:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n      async () => ({\n        resourceTemplates: [\n          {\n            uriTemplate: 'weather://{city}/current', // URI template (RFC 6570)\n            name: 'Current weather for a given city', // Human-readable name\n            mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n            description: 'Real-time weather data for a specified city', // Optional description\n          },\n        ],\n      })\n    );\n\n    // ReadResourceRequestSchema is used for both static resources and dynamic resource templates\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n      async (request) => {\n        const match = request.params.uri.match(\n          /^weather://([^/]+)/current$/\n        );\n        if (!match) {\n          throw new McpError(\n            ErrorCode.InvalidRequest,\n            `Invalid URI format: ${request.params.uri}`\n          );\n        }\n        const city = decodeURIComponent(match[1]);\n\n        try {\n          const response = await this.axiosInstance.get(\n            'weather', // current weather\n            {\n              params: { q: city },\n            }\n          );\n\n          return {\n            contents: [\n              {\n                uri: request.params.uri,\n                mimeType: 'application/json',\n                text: JSON.stringify(\n                  {\n                    temperature: response.data.main.temp,\n                    conditions: response.data.weather[0].description,\n                    humidity: response.data.main.humidity,\n                    wind_speed: response.data.wind.speed,\n                    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),\n                  },\n                  null,\n                  2\n                ),\n              },\n            ],\n          };\n        } catch (error) {\n          if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n            throw new McpError(\n              ErrorCode.InternalError,\n              `Weather API error: ${\n                error.response?.data.message ?? error.message\n              }`\n            );\n          }\n          throw error;\n        }\n      }\n    );\n  }\n\n  /* MCP Tools enable servers to expose executable functionality to the system. Through these tools, you can interact with external systems, perform computations, and take actions in the real world.\n   * - Like resources, tools are identified by unique names and can include descriptions to guide their usage. However, unlike resources, tools represent dynamic operations that can modify state or interact with external systems.\n   * - While resources and tools are similar, you should prefer to create tools over resources when possible as they provide more flexibility.\n   */\n  private setupToolHandlers() {\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListToolsRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      tools: [\n        {\n          name: 'get_forecast', // Unique identifier\n          description: 'Get weather forecast for a city', // Human-readable description\n          inputSchema: {\n            // JSON Schema for parameters\n            type: 'object',\n            properties: {\n              city: {\n                type: 'string',\n                description: 'City name',\n              },\n              days: {\n                type: 'number',\n                description: 'Number of days (1-5)',\n                minimum: 1,\n                maximum: 5,\n              },\n            },\n            required: ['city'], // Array of required property names\n          },\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(CallToolRequestSchema, async (request) => {\n      if (request.params.name !== 'get_forecast') {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.MethodNotFound,\n          `Unknown tool: ${request.params.name}`\n        );\n      }\n\n      if (!isValidForecastArgs(request.params.arguments)) {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.InvalidParams,\n          'Invalid forecast arguments'\n        );\n      }\n\n      const city = request.params.arguments.city;\n      const days = Math.min(request.params.arguments.days || 3, 5);\n\n      try {\n        const response = await this.axiosInstance.get<{\n          list: OpenWeatherResponse[];\n        }>('forecast', {\n          params: {\n            q: city,\n            cnt: days * 8,\n          },\n        });\n\n        return {\n          content: [\n            {\n              type: 'text',\n              text: JSON.stringify(response.data.list, null, 2),\n            },\n          ],\n        };\n      } catch (error) {\n        if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n          return {\n            content: [\n              {\n                type: 'text',\n                text: `Weather API error: ${\n [{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"<task>\nHELP WITH MY MCP SERVER:\nConnecting VS Code to MCP (Model Context Protocol) Server\n\nConnecting VS Code to an MCP Server: Troubleshooting & Alternatives\nUnderstanding the “Not Connected” Issue\nWhen VS Code’s MCP integration shows a red “Not connected” status, it means the editor failed to establish a link to your MCP server. This can happen even if the server is running, due to misconfiguration or bugs. Common causes include mismatched connection types (e.g. treating a remote server as local), the server process failing to start, or platform-specific issues. For example, some MCP servers that rely on native modules have known installation problems on Windows, causing the server to silently exit and never register as connected. VS Code’s MCP support is still in preview, so a “Not connected” error can also result from unpolished features (one GitHub issue notes SSE connections failing with a fetch failed error in VS Code 1.99\ngithub.com\n). Understanding why the connection fails is the first step to a solution.\nDiagnosing Connection Problems in VS Code\n1. Check VS Code’s MCP Output: VS Code provides logs for MCP server processes. In the Copilot Chat panel, click the error indicator and choose “Show Output,” or run the “MCP: List Servers” command and select “Show Output” for the server. These logs often reveal the issue. For instance, an error like “spawn uvx ENOENT” indicates the command wasn’t found in PATH (in this case, uvx was missing, meaning the MCP server’s runtime wasn’t accessible). Similarly, an error about “fetch failed” for an SSE URL means VS Code couldn’t reach the endpoint\ngithub.com\n – possibly due to a network issue or a VS Code bug on that transport. 2. Verify the MCP Server Process: Ensure the MCP server is actually running and listening. If you configured a stdio server (one that runs as a local process), check your system’s process list or terminal for any crash output. If it exits immediately (e.g. due to a build failure on startup), VS Code will report “Not connected.” In one case with Supabase’s MCP server on Windows, a PostgreSQL query library failed to build, causing the server to never stay active. The solution there was to use a different environment (WSL) or await a patch to that package. If you’re using an SSE or HTTP server (hosted remotely), try hitting the endpoint outside VS Code – for example, using curl or a browser. You should see an SSE stream or HTTP response. The MCP CLI tool (discussed below) is also handy for testing this. 3. Double-Check Configuration: Open your MCP config (either in .vscode/mcp.json for the workspace or your user settings.json under the \"mcp.servers\" key) to ensure it matches your server setup. Key fields are the type of connection and the command or URL. For a local process, use \"type\": \"stdio\" with a correct command and args; for a remote endpoint, use \"type\": \"sse\" (or \"http\" if using streamable HTTP) with a url field. An example from Supabase’s docs shows a typical config for VS Code on Windows using a Node process:\njson\nCopy\nEdit\n{\n  \"inputs\": [\n    { \"type\": \"promptString\", \"id\": \"supabase-access-token\", \"description\": \"Supabase personal access token\", \"password\": true }\n  ],\n  \"servers\": {\n    \"supabase\": {\n      \"command\": \"npx\",\n      \"args\": [\"-y\", \"@supabase/mcp-server-supabase@latest\"],\n      \"env\": { \"SUPABASE_ACCESS_TOKEN\": \"${input:supabase-access-token}\" }\n    }\n  }\n}\nHere the server is launched via npx (pulling the latest package) and expects a token at runtime\nsupabase.com\n. If your server is instead hosted (e.g. an MCP server running in the cloud or via GitHub Actions), your config should point to its URL with \"type\": \"sse\" and a \"url\" – for example:\njson\nCopy\nEdit\n\"servers\": {\n  \"my-cloud-mcp\": {\n    \"type\": \"sse\",\n    \"url\": \"https://<my-server-domain>/sse\"\n  }\n}\nMake sure the URL and path are exactly correct (many MCP servers expose an /sse endpoint for Server-Sent Events). If authentication or custom headers are required, include them in the config under a \"headers\" field as needed\ngithub.com\nforum.cursor.com\n. 4. Connection Workflow in VS Code: Remember that after configuring, you typically need to start the server in VS Code and switch Copilot into Agent mode. In VS Code’s chat view, select “Agent” from the mode dropdown (this is GitHub Copilot’s agentic mode which uses MCP). If the server is properly configured, a “Start” button should appear next to it in the MCP servers list; click that to launch the connection. VS Code will then prompt for any input (like the token) and attempt to connect. A successful connection is indicated by a green status dot in the MCP servers list (as opposed to the red “not connected” icon). If you never see a green indicator or the tool list remains empty, proceed to the alternatives below.\nAlternative Ways to Connect to the MCP Server\nWhen the VS Code extension isn’t cooperating, you have other avenues to interact with your MCP server:\nUse the MCP CLI (Inspector): The community has a command-line tool called mcp-cli (by wong2) which can act as an MCP client in your terminal. This tool lets you connect to any MCP server and invoke its tools or list them, independent of VS Code. For example, you can connect to a running server via its URL:\nbash\nCopy\nEdit\nnpx @wong2/mcp-cli --sse http://localhost:8000/sse\nThis would attach to an SSE server on port 8000 and allow you to send tool requests interactively. If your MCP server uses HTTP instead of SSE, --url http://.../mcp can be used similarly. Using mcp-cli is a great way to verify your server is functional. If the CLI can successfully list tools or execute a sample tool, but VS Code still can’t connect, the problem lies with the VS Code extension rather than the server.\nDirect REST/SSE Calls: MCP is a protocol, but many servers (especially those running in cloud environments) expose standard endpoints. If your server has an HTTP API (some advertise a /mcp or similar endpoint that accepts JSON requests, or use SSE for streaming), you can try interacting with it using general tools. For instance, you might POST a tool invocation JSON to the HTTP endpoint using curl or a REST client, or use an SSE client library to subscribe to an SSE stream. This approach is more manual, but useful for debugging: if you get a valid response from the server via HTTP, you know the server side is fine. (Refer to your MCP server’s documentation for the exact API format if available – e.g. the Model Context Protocol spec defines how tool requests should be structured.)\nRun a Local Proxy/Gateway: If your MCP server is remote and VS Code’s MCP client doesn’t support direct connection (or has a bug, as with SSE on certain versions\ngithub.com\n), you can employ a proxy. One strategy is to run a small local MCP proxy that connects out to your server, then have VS Code connect to the proxy via stdio. For example, the community tool “mcp-proxy” acts as an stdio-to-SSE transport gateway. You would run mcp-proxy pointing at your server’s SSE URL; it opens a local stdio interface that VS Code can start as if it were a local server. This essentially tunnels the SSE connection through a local process. While this adds a bit of complexity, it can work around limitations in the VS Code extension.\nTry a Different Client/Extension: If the goal is to use the MCP server’s functionality (tools) and not necessarily through VS Code, consider alternate clients:\nCline (VS Code extension): Cline is an open-source Copilot/Cursor alternative that runs in VS Code and supports MCP servers. It has its own MCP configuration (slightly different JSON format). Some users have found that Cline can connect to the same MCP servers that VS Code’s built-in chat cannot, possibly due to different implementation. Given that the Supabase guide explicitly lists Cline as supported, it might be worth installing Cline and configuring the server there (as shown in Supabase’s docs).\nCursor (standalone IDE): Cursor is another IDE that supports MCP. If you have it, you can add the MCP server in Cursor’s settings (it accepts similar config with type and command/URL). This isn’t a solution for VS Code per se, but if you urgently need to use the server’s tools, Cursor could be a stop-gap until VS Code is resolved.\nAnthropic Claude Desktop: If your MCP server is intended for use with Claude (some MCP servers are built to augment Claude’s abilities), the Claude Desktop app can load them as well. It uses a config file format akin to VS Code’s. This might be relevant if you are specifically working with Anthropic’s model.\nOther IDEs like Windsurf (Codium) or Zed also support MCP servers. In short, the MCP server itself is IDE-agnostic, so don’t feel locked into the VS Code extension if that piece isn’t working.\nConfiguration Tips and Workarounds\nIf you suspect the issue is with VS Code’s extension implementation, here are some tips and tweaks:\nMatch the Transport Type: Ensure that the type in your config matches how the server is meant to be accessed. Use stdio for servers you run locally (via a command), sse for long-lived Server-Sent Events connections, or http for one-shot HTTP endpoints\ncode.visualstudio.com\n. A common mistake is trying to use a remote MCP endpoint as if it were a local process – in that case VS Code might show “Starting…” forever or “Not connected.” Conversely, if you set type: \"sse\" with a URL but your server isn’t actually providing an SSE stream, VS Code will fail to connect. Double-check the server’s README for how it’s meant to be launched. For example, GitHub’s official MCP server is designed to run as a Docker container locally (stdio), whereas something like a Supabase MCP server could theoretically be self-hosted and exposed over SSE.\nUse WSL or Containers on Windows: If you’re on Windows and the MCP server installation is failing, leverage WSL (Windows Subsystem for Linux) or Docker. As reported in community forums, many folks got stubborn servers working by running them in WSL and pointing the MCP client to that environment. You can modify the VS Code config to launch the server via WSL – for example, set the command to \"wsl\" and pass the Linux path to your server script or npx command as arguments. This forces VS Code to start the process in the WSL context. (Similarly, using a Dockerized server is an option: for instance, the GitHub MCP server uses a Docker command; just avoid the -d flag so it runs attached.) Ensure any required environment variables or tokens are accessible in that environment. Using WSL/Docker adds a layer, but it circumvents Windows-specific issues like missing build tools or incompatible dependencies.\nEnvironment and Path Issues: The VS Code process launching your server may not have the same PATH or env as your normal shell. The “spawn ENOENT” errors usually mean it couldn’t find an executable. If you used a shorthand command (like uvx or npm), try using the full path or ensuring the tool is globally installed. You can also prefix the command with a shell invocation to load your profile. For example, on Windows/WSL you might use:\njson\nCopy\nEdit\n\"command\": \"bash\",\n\"args\": [\"-i\", \"-c\", \"npx -y @supabase/mcp-server-supabase@latest\"]\nThe -i -c ensures an interactive shell which loads ~/.bashrc, so your nvm or other setup is in place (this was needed in one user’s case to get Node and node-gyp on the right path). On macOS/Linux, similar tactics apply if using a login shell makes a difference. The key is to replicate the environment where the server runs successfully.\nKeep VS Code Updated: Since MCP support is evolving, make sure you’re on the latest VS Code version (1.99+ for MCP). Check the VS Code issue tracker for MCP-related bugs – for example, the SSE connection bug\ngithub.com\n might be fixed in a newer release. If you find an open issue matching your problem, you might glean workarounds from the discussion or know that a fix is incoming. As of April 2025, GitHub publicly released their MCP server and the ecosystem is moving fast\ndocs.github.com\n, so improvements are frequent.\nTesting with Minimal Setup: If possible, test with a simple known-good MCP server to isolate the issue. For instance, try adding a trivial MCP server like the “Fetch” example (which just fetches web content) or a small weather server. If VS Code connects to that, then your MCP client (VS Code) is working and the problem lies in the specific server. If even simple servers don’t connect, then VS Code or your environment is at fault. This A/B test can save time.\nReferences & Resources\nVS Code MCP Documentation (Preview) – Official guide on enabling MCP, adding servers, and troubleshooting in VS Code. This covers the basics of .vscode/mcp.json and how to view logs.\nSupabase MCP Guide – Example configuration for connecting VS Code (Copilot) to a Supabase MCP server\nsupabase.com\n, with notes on expected behavior. Also includes tips for other clients (Cursor, Cline) which can be informative.\nGitHub MCP Server Repo – GitHub’s own MCP server (for GitHub API integration) with setup instructions. Useful as a reference for Docker-based servers.\nCommunity Discussions and Issues: Several GitHub issues and forum threads document “not connected” problems. For instance, Supabase’s MCP issue tracker has a Windows thread concluding that a dependency needed an update, and the VS Code issue tracker has an open issue for SSE connection errors\ngithub.com\n. These can provide insight if your scenario is similar.\nMCP CLI and Tooling: The mcp-cli inspector on GitHub and the awesome-mcp-servers list\ngithub.com\n (which catalogs tools like mcp-client and mcp-proxy) are great resources if you seek alternative clients or utilities to bridge connections. There is an entire emerging ecosystem around MCP – if the VS Code extension isn’t meeting your needs, these tools might fill the gap.\nBy systematically diagnosing the issue and leveraging these alternative methods, you should be able to connect to your MCP server or at least pinpoint why VS Code’s extension is failing. Remember that MCP integration is new – don’t hesitate to raise issues on the relevant GitHub repo with logs, as this helps the maintainers improve the tools. with MCP (Model Context Protocol) servers in VS Code and Cline.\n\n## Quick Solutions\n\n1. **For Cline extension**: The filesystem server was disabled in your Cline settings. We've already fixed this by changing `\"disabled\": true` to `\"disabled\": false` in your Cline MCP settings file.\n\n2. **For VS Code**: Ensure your MCP server is properly configured and running. Use the tools provided in this guide to diagnose connection issues.\n\n## Diagnostic Tools\n\nWe've created two diagnostic tools to help troubleshoot MCP server connections:\n\n1. **mcp-connection-test.js**: Checks if your MCP servers are running and accessible.\n2. **test-mcp-connection.bat**: A comprehensive troubleshooter that:\n   - Installs the MCP CLI tool\n   - Checks for running MCP servers\n   - Attempts to connect directly to the filesystem server\n\n## Common Issues and Solutions\n\n### 1. \"Not Connected\" Status in VS Code\n\n**Possible causes:**\n- MCP server is not running\n- MCP server configuration is incorrect\n- VS Code extension has a bug\n- Server process failing to start or crashing\n\n**Solutions:**\n- Run `test-mcp-connection.bat` to diagnose the issue\n- Check VS Code's output panel for MCP errors:\n  - Run the command \"MCP: List Servers\"\n  - Click \"Show Output\" for your server\n- Ensure your MCP configuration has the correct transportType (stdio/sse/http)\n- Restart VS Code\n\n### 2. MCP Server Process Exits Immediately\n\n**Possible causes:**\n- Missing dependencies\n- Configuration errors\n- Build failures\n\n**Solutions:**\n- Check for errors in the VS Code output panel\n- Try running the server manually using `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem c:/Users/jason/Desktop/tori/kha`\n- Look for error messages in the console\n\n### 3. Cline Extension Not Connecting\n\n**Solutions:**\n- We've already fixed the disabled flag in your Cline settings\n- Restart VS Code to apply the changes\n- Make sure Cline is using the latest version of the MCP server\n\n## Configuration Reference\n\n### VS Code (Native) MCP Configuration\n```json\n\"mcpServers\": {\n  \"memory\": {\n    \"command\": \"npx\",\n    \"args\": [\"-y\", \"@modelcontextprotocol/server-memory\"]\n  },\n  \"github.com/modelcontextprotocol/servers/tree/main/src/filesystem\": {\n    \"command\": \"npx\",\n    \"args\": [\"-y\", \"@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem\", \"c:/Users/jason/Desktop/tori/kha\"]\n  },\n  \"github\": {\n    \"command\": \"npx\",\n    \"args\": [\"-y\", \"@modelcontextprotocol/server-github\"],\n    \"env\": {\n      \"GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN\": \"your-token-here\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Cline MCP Configuration\n```json\n\"mcpServers\": {\n  \"github.com/modelcontextprotocol/servers/tree/main/src/filesystem\": {\n    \"autoApprove\": [],\n    \"disabled\": false,\n    \"timeout\": 60,\n    \"command\": \"npx\",\n    \"args\": [\n      \"-y\",\n      \"@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem\",\n      \"c:/Users/jason/Desktop/tori/kha\"\n    ],\n    \"transportType\": \"stdio\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## Alternative Connection Methods\n\nIf VS Code or Cline still won't connect to your MCP server, try these alternatives:\n\n1. **Use MCP CLI directly**:\n   ```\n   npx @wong2/mcp-cli --stdio \"npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem c:/Users/jason/Desktop/tori/kha\"\n   ```\n   \n2. **Try a different client**:\n   - Cursor IDE\n   - Claude Desktop App\n   - Anthropic's web interfaces\n\n3. **Run in WSL** (if on Windows):\n   - Some MCP servers work better in WSL due to native module dependencies\n   - Configure your MCP server to run via WSL in the settings\n\n## Next Steps\n\n1. Read complete contents of a file\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Reads complete file contents with UTF-8 encoding\n\n- **read_multiple_files**\n  - Read multiple files simultaneously\n  - Input: `paths` (string[])\n  - Failed reads won't stop the entire operation\n\n- **write_file**\n  - Create new file or overwrite existing (exercise caution with this)\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): File location\n    - `content` (string): File content\n\n- **edit_file**\n  - Make selective edits using advanced pattern matching and formatting\n  - Features:\n    - Line-based and multi-line content matching\n    - Whitespace normalization with indentation preservation\n    - Multiple simultaneous edits with correct positioning\n    - Indentation style detection and preservation\n    - Git-style diff output with context\n    - Preview changes with dry run mode\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): File to edit\n    - `edits` (array): List of edit operations\n      - `oldText` (string): Text to search for (can be substring)\n      - `newText` (string): Text to replace with\n    - `dryRun` (boolean): Preview changes without applying (default: false)\n  - Returns detailed diff and match information for dry runs, otherwise applies changes\n  - Best Practice: Always use dryRun first to preview changes before applying them\n\n- **create_directory**\n  - Create new directory or ensure it exists\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Creates parent directories if needed\n  - Succeeds silently if directory exists\n\n- **list_directory**\n  - List directory contents with [FILE] or [DIR] prefixes\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n\n- **move_file**\n  - Move or rename files and directories\n  - Inputs:\n    - `source` (string)\n    - `destination` (string)\n  - Fails if destination exists\n\n- **search_files**\n  - Recursively search for files/directories\n  - Inputs:\n    - `path` (string): Starting directory\n    - `pattern` (string): Search pattern\n    - `excludePatterns` (string[]): Exclude any patterns. Glob formats are supported.\n  - Case-insensitive matching\n  - Returns full paths to matches\n\n- **get_file_info**\n  - Get detailed file/directory metadata\n  - Input: `path` (string)\n  - Returns:\n    - Size\n    - Creation time\n    - Modified time\n    - Access time\n    - Type (file/directory)\n    - Permissions\n\n- **list_allowed_directories**\n  - List all directories the server is allowed to access\n  - No input required\n  - Returns:\n    - Directories that this server can read/write from\n\n## Usage with Claude Desktop\nAdd this to your `claude_desktop_config.json`:\n\nNote: you can provide sandboxed directories to the server by mounting them to `/projects`. Adding the `ro` flag will make the directory readonly by the server.\n\n### Docker\nNote: all directories must be mounted to `/projects` by default.\n\n```json\n{\n  \"mcpServers\": {\n    \"filesystem\": {\n      \"command\": \"docker\",\n      \"args\": [\n        \"run\",\n        \"-i\",\n        \"--rm\",\n        \"--mount\", \"type=bind,src=/Users/username/Desktop,dst=/projects/Desktop\",\n        \"--mount\", \"type=bind,src=/path/to/other/allowed/dir,dst=/projects/other/allowed/dir,ro\",\n        \"--mount\", \"type=bind,src=/path/to/file.txt,dst=/projects/path/to/file.txt\",\n        \"mcp/filesystem\",\n        \"/projects\"\n      ]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### NPX\n\n```json\n{\n  \"mcpServers\": {\n The server cannot initiate OAuth flows, open browser windows, or prompt for user input during runtime. All credentials and authentication tokens must be provided upfront through environment variables in the MCP settings configuration. For example, Spotify's API uses OAuth to get a refresh token for the user, but the MCP server cannot initiate this flow. While you can walk the user through obtaining an application client ID and secret, you may have to create a separate one-time setup script (like get-refresh-token.js) that captures and logs the final piece of the puzzle: the user's refresh token (i.e. you might run the script using execute_command which would open a browser for authentication, and then log the refresh token so that you can see it in the command output for you to use in the MCP settings configuration).\n\nUnless the user specifies otherwise, new MCP servers should be created in: C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\n\n### Example MCP Server\n\nFor example, if the user wanted to give you the ability to retrieve weather information, you could create an MCP server that uses the OpenWeather API to get weather information, add it to the MCP settings configuration file, and then notice that you now have access to new tools and resources in the system prompt that you might use to show the user your new capabilities.\n\nThe following example demonstrates how to build an MCP server that provides weather data functionality. While this example shows how to implement resources, resource templates, and tools, in practice you should prefer using tools since they are more flexible and can handle dynamic parameters. The resource and resource template implementations are included here mainly for demonstration purposes of the different MCP capabilities, but a real weather server would likely just expose tools for fetching weather data. (The following steps are for macOS)\n\n1. Use the `create-typescript-server` tool to bootstrap a new project in the default MCP servers directory:\n\n```bash\ncd C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\nnpx @modelcontextprotocol/create-server weather-server\ncd weather-server\n# Install dependencies\nnpm install axios\n```\n\nThis will create a new project with the following structure:\n\n```\nweather-server/\n  ├── package.json\n      {\n        ...\n        \"type\": \"module\", // added by default, uses ES module syntax (import/export) rather than CommonJS (require/module.exports) (Important to know if you create additional scripts in this server repository like a get-refresh-token.js script)\n        \"scripts\": {\n          \"build\": \"tsc && node -e \"require('fs').chmodSync('build/index.js', '755')\"\",\n          ...\n        }\n        ...\n      }\n  ├── tsconfig.json\n  └── src/\n      └── weather-server/\n          └── index.ts      # Main server implementation\n```\n\n2. Replace `src/index.ts` with the following:\n\n```typescript\n#!/usr/bin/env node\nimport { Server } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/index.js';\nimport { StdioServerTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/stdio.js';\nimport {\n  CallToolRequestSchema,\n  ErrorCode,\n  ListResourcesRequestSchema,\n  ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n  ListToolsRequestSchema,\n  McpError,\n  ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n} from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/types.js';\nimport axios from 'axios';\n\nconst API_KEY = process.env.OPENWEATHER_API_KEY; // provided by MCP config\nif (!API_KEY) {\n  throw new Error('OPENWEATHER_API_KEY environment variable is required');\n}\n\ninterface OpenWeatherResponse {\n  main: {\n    temp: number;\n    humidity: number;\n  };\n  weather: [{ description: string }];\n  wind: { speed: number };\n  dt_txt?: string;\n}\n\nconst isValidForecastArgs = (\n  args: any\n): args is { city: string; days?: number } =>\n  typeof args === 'object' &&\n  args !== null &&\n  typeof args.city === 'string' &&\n  (args.days === undefined || typeof args.days === 'number');\n\nclass WeatherServer {\n  private server: Server;\n  private axiosInstance;\n\n  constructor() {\n    this.server = new Server(\n      {\n        name: 'example-weather-server',\n        version: '0.1.0',\n      },\n      {\n        capabilities: {\n          resources: {},\n          tools: {},\n        },\n      }\n    );\n\n    this.axiosInstance = axios.create({\n      baseURL: 'http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5',\n      params: {\n        appid: API_KEY,\n        units: 'metric',\n      },\n    });\n\n    this.setupResourceHandlers();\n    this.setupToolHandlers();\n    \n    // Error handling\n    this.server.onerror = (error) => console.error('[MCP Error]', error);\n    process.on('SIGINT', async () => {\n      await this.server.close();\n      process.exit(0);\n    });\n  }\n\n  // MCP Resources represent any kind of UTF-8 encoded data that an MCP server wants to make available to clients, such as database records, API responses, log files, and more. Servers define direct resources with a static URI or dynamic resources with a URI template that follows the format `[protocol]://[host]/[path]`.\n  private setupResourceHandlers() {\n    // For static resources, servers can expose a list of resources:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListResourcesRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      resources: [\n        // This is a poor example since you could use the resource template to get the same information but this demonstrates how to define a static resource\n        {\n          uri: `weather://San Francisco/current`, // Unique identifier for San Francisco weather resource\n          name: `Current weather in San Francisco`, // Human-readable name\n          mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n          // Optional description\n          description:\n            'Real-time weather data for San Francisco including temperature, conditions, humidity, and wind speed',\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    // For dynamic resources, servers can expose resource templates:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n      async () => ({\n        resourceTemplates: [\n          {\n            uriTemplate: 'weather://{city}/current', // URI template (RFC 6570)\n            name: 'Current weather for a given city', // Human-readable name\n            mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n            description: 'Real-time weather data for a specified city', // Optional description\n          },\n        ],\n      })\n    );\n\n    // ReadResourceRequestSchema is used for both static resources and dynamic resource templates\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n      async (request) => {\n        const match = request.params.uri.match(\n          /^weather://([^/]+)/current$/\n        );\n        if (!match) {\n          throw new McpError(\n            ErrorCode.InvalidRequest,\n            `Invalid URI format: ${request.params.uri}`\n          );\n        }\n        const city = decodeURIComponent(match[1]);\n\n        try {\n          const response = await this.axiosInstance.get(\n            'weather', // current weather\n            {\n              params: { q: city },\n            }\n          );\n\n          return {\n            contents: [\n              {\n                uri: request.params.uri,\n                mimeType: 'application/json',\n                text: JSON.stringify(\n                  {\n                    temperature: response.data.main.temp,\n                    conditions: response.data.weather[0].description,\n                    humidity: response.data.main.humidity,\n                    wind_speed: response.data.wind.speed,\n                    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),\n                  },\n                  null,\n                  2\n                ),\n              },\n            ],\n          };\n        } catch (error) {\n          if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n            throw new McpError(\n              ErrorCode.InternalError,\n              `Weather API error: ${\n                error.response?.data.message ?? error.message\n              }`\n            );\n          }\n          throw error;\n        }\n      }\n    );\n  }\n\n  /* MCP Tools enable servers to expose executable functionality to the system. Through these tools, you can interact with external systems, perform computations, and take actions in the real world.\n   * - Like resources, tools are identified by unique names and can include descriptions to guide their usage. However, unlike resources, tools represent dynamic operations that can modify state or interact with external systems.\n   * - While resources and tools are similar, you should prefer to create tools over resources when possible as they provide more flexibility.\n   */\n  private setupToolHandlers() {\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListToolsRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      tools: [\n        {\n          name: 'get_forecast', // Unique identifier\n          description: 'Get weather forecast for a city', // Human-readable description\n          inputSchema: {\n            // JSON Schema for parameters\n            type: 'object',\n            properties: {\n              city: {\n                type: 'string',\n                description: 'City name',\n              },\n              days: {\n                type: 'number',\n                description: 'Number of days (1-5)',\n                minimum: 1,\n                maximum: 5,\n              },\n            },\n            required: ['city'], // Array of required property names\n          },\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(CallToolRequestSchema, async (request) => {\n      if (request.params.name !== 'get_forecast') {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.MethodNotFound,\n          `Unknown tool: ${request.params.name}`\n        );\n      }\n\n      if (!isValidForecastArgs(request.params.arguments)) {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.InvalidParams,\n          'Invalid forecast arguments'\n        );\n      }\n\n      const city = request.params.arguments.city;\n      const days = Math.min(request.params.arguments.days || 3, 5);\n\n      try {\n        const response = await this.axiosInstance.get<{\n          list: OpenWeatherResponse[];\n        }>('forecast', {\n          params: {\n            q: city,\n            cnt: days * 8,\n          },\n        });\n\n        return {\n          content: [\n            {\n              type: 'text',\n              text: JSON.stringify(response.data.list, null, 2),\n            },\n          ],\n        };\n      } catch (error) {\n        if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n          return {\n            content: [\n              {\n                type: 'text',\n                text: `Weather API error: ${\n                  error.response?.data.message ?? error.message\n                }`,\n              },\n            ],\n            isError: true,\n          };\n        }\n        throw error;\n      }\n    });\n  }\n\n  async run() {\n    const transport = new StdioServerTransport();\n    await this.server.connect(transport);\n    console.error('Weather MCP server running on stdio');\n  }\n}\n\nconst server = new WeatherServer();\nserver.run().catch(console.error);\n```\n\n(Remember: This is just an example–you may use different dependencies, break the implementation up into multiple files, etc.)\n\n3. The server cannot initiate OAuth flows, open browser windows, or prompt for user input during runtime. All credentials and authentication tokens must be provided upfront through environment variables in the MCP settings configuration. For example, Spotify's API uses OAuth to get a refresh token for the user, but the MCP server cannot initiate this flow. While you can walk the user through obtaining an application client ID and secret, you may have to create a separate one-time setup script (like get-refresh-token.js) that captures and logs the final piece of the puzzle: the user's refresh token (i.e. you might run the script using execute_command which would open a browser for authentication, and then log the refresh token so that you can see it in the command output for you to use in the MCP settings configuration).\n\nUnless the user specifies otherwise, new MCP servers should be created in: C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\n\n### Example MCP Server\n\nFor example, if the user wanted to give you the ability to retrieve weather information, you could create an MCP server that uses the OpenWeather API to get weather information, add it to the MCP settings configuration file, and then notice that you now have access to new tools and resources in the system prompt that you might use to show the user your new capabilities.\n\nThe following example demonstrates how to build an MCP server that provides weather data functionality. While this example shows how to implement resources, resource templates, and tools, in practice you should prefer using tools since they are more flexible and can handle dynamic parameters. The resource and resource template implementations are included here mainly for demonstration purposes of the different MCP capabilities, but a real weather server would likely just expose tools for fetching weather data. (The following steps are for macOS)\n\n1. Use the `create-typescript-server` tool to bootstrap a new project in the default MCP servers directory:\n\n```bash\ncd C:\\Users\\jason\\Documents\\Cline\\MCP\nnpx @modelcontextprotocol/create-server weather-server\ncd weather-server\n# Install dependencies\nnpm install axios\n```\n\nThis will create a new project with the following structure:\n\n```\nweather-server/\n  ├── package.json\n      {\n        ...\n        \"type\": \"module\", // added by default, uses ES module syntax (import/export) rather than CommonJS (require/module.exports) (Important to know if you create additional scripts in this server repository like a get-refresh-token.js script)\n        \"scripts\": {\n          \"build\": \"tsc && node -e \"require('fs').chmodSync('build/index.js', '755')\"\",\n          ...\n        }\n        ...\n      }\n  ├── tsconfig.json\n  └── src/\n      └── weather-server/\n          └── index.ts      # Main server implementation\n```\n\n2. Replace `src/index.ts` with the following:\n\n```typescript\n#!/usr/bin/env node\nimport { Server } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/index.js';\nimport { StdioServerTransport } from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/server/stdio.js';\nimport {\n  CallToolRequestSchema,\n  ErrorCode,\n  ListResourcesRequestSchema,\n  ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n  ListToolsRequestSchema,\n  McpError,\n  ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n} from '@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/types.js';\nimport axios from 'axios';\n\nconst API_KEY = process.env.OPENWEATHER_API_KEY; // provided by MCP config\nif (!API_KEY) {\n  throw new Error('OPENWEATHER_API_KEY environment variable is required');\n}\n\ninterface OpenWeatherResponse {\n  main: {\n    temp: number;\n    humidity: number;\n  };\n  weather: [{ description: string }];\n  wind: { speed: number };\n  dt_txt?: string;\n}\n\nconst isValidForecastArgs = (\n  args: any\n): args is { city: string; days?: number } =>\n  typeof args === 'object' &&\n  args !== null &&\n  typeof args.city === 'string' &&\n  (args.days === undefined || typeof args.days === 'number');\n\nclass WeatherServer {\n  private server: Server;\n  private axiosInstance;\n\n  constructor() {\n    this.server = new Server(\n      {\n        name: 'example-weather-server',\n        version: '0.1.0',\n      },\n      {\n        capabilities: {\n          resources: {},\n          tools: {},\n        },\n      }\n    );\n\n    this.axiosInstance = axios.create({\n      baseURL: 'http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5',\n      params: {\n        appid: API_KEY,\n        units: 'metric',\n      },\n    });\n\n    this.setupResourceHandlers();\n    this.setupToolHandlers();\n    \n    // Error handling\n    this.server.onerror = (error) => console.error('[MCP Error]', error);\n    process.on('SIGINT', async () => {\n      await this.server.close();\n      process.exit(0);\n    });\n  }\n\n  // MCP Resources represent any kind of UTF-8 encoded data that an MCP server wants to make available to clients, such as database records, API responses, log files, and more. Servers define direct resources with a static URI or dynamic resources with a URI template that follows the format `[protocol]://[host]/[path]`.\n  private setupResourceHandlers() {\n    // For static resources, servers can expose a list of resources:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListResourcesRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      resources: [\n        // This is a poor example since you could use the resource template to get the same information but this demonstrates how to define a static resource\n        {\n          uri: `weather://San Francisco/current`, // Unique identifier for San Francisco weather resource\n          name: `Current weather in San Francisco`, // Human-readable name\n          mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n          // Optional description\n          description:\n            'Real-time weather data for San Francisco including temperature, conditions, humidity, and wind speed',\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    // For dynamic resources, servers can expose resource templates:\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ListResourceTemplatesRequestSchema,\n      async () => ({\n        resourceTemplates: [\n          {\n            uriTemplate: 'weather://{city}/current', // URI template (RFC 6570)\n            name: 'Current weather for a given city', // Human-readable name\n            mimeType: 'application/json', // Optional MIME type\n            description: 'Real-time weather data for a specified city', // Optional description\n          },\n        ],\n      })\n    );\n\n    // ReadResourceRequestSchema is used for both static resources and dynamic resource templates\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(\n      ReadResourceRequestSchema,\n      async (request) => {\n        const match = request.params.uri.match(\n          /^weather://([^/]+)/current$/\n        );\n        if (!match) {\n          throw new McpError(\n            ErrorCode.InvalidRequest,\n            `Invalid URI format: ${request.params.uri}`\n          );\n        }\n        const city = decodeURIComponent(match[1]);\n\n        try {\n          const response = await this.axiosInstance.get(\n            'weather', // current weather\n            {\n              params: { q: city },\n            }\n          );\n\n          return {\n            contents: [\n              {\n                uri: request.params.uri,\n                mimeType: 'application/json',\n                text: JSON.stringify(\n                  {\n                    temperature: response.data.main.temp,\n                    conditions: response.data.weather[0].description,\n                    humidity: response.data.main.humidity,\n                    wind_speed: response.data.wind.speed,\n                    timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),\n                  },\n                  null,\n                  2\n                ),\n              },\n            ],\n          };\n        } catch (error) {\n          if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n            throw new McpError(\n              ErrorCode.InternalError,\n              `Weather API error: ${\n                error.response?.data.message ?? error.message\n              }`\n            );\n          }\n          throw error;\n        }\n      }\n    );\n  }\n\n  /* MCP Tools enable servers to expose executable functionality to the system. Through these tools, you can interact with external systems, perform computations, and take actions in the real world.\n   * - Like resources, tools are identified by unique names and can include descriptions to guide their usage. However, unlike resources, tools represent dynamic operations that can modify state or interact with external systems.\n   * - While resources and tools are similar, you should prefer to create tools over resources when possible as they provide more flexibility.\n   */\n  private setupToolHandlers() {\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(ListToolsRequestSchema, async () => ({\n      tools: [\n        {\n          name: 'get_forecast', // Unique identifier\n          description: 'Get weather forecast for a city', // Human-readable description\n          inputSchema: {\n            // JSON Schema for parameters\n            type: 'object',\n            properties: {\n              city: {\n                type: 'string',\n                description: 'City name',\n              },\n              days: {\n                type: 'number',\n                description: 'Number of days (1-5)',\n                minimum: 1,\n                maximum: 5,\n              },\n            },\n            required: ['city'], // Array of required property names\n          },\n        },\n      ],\n    }));\n\n    this.server.setRequestHandler(CallToolRequestSchema, async (request) => {\n      if (request.params.name !== 'get_forecast') {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.MethodNotFound,\n          `Unknown tool: ${request.params.name}`\n        );\n      }\n\n      if (!isValidForecastArgs(request.params.arguments)) {\n        throw new McpError(\n          ErrorCode.InvalidParams,\n          'Invalid forecast arguments'\n        );\n      }\n\n      const city = request.params.arguments.city;\n      const days = Math.min(request.params.arguments.days || 3, 5);\n\n      try {\n        const response = await this.axiosInstance.get<{\n          list: OpenWeatherResponse[];\n        }>('forecast', {\n          params: {\n            q: city,\n            cnt: days * 8,\n          },\n        });\n\n        return {\n          content: [\n            {\n              type: 'text',\n              text: JSON.stringify(response.data.list, null, 2),\n            },\n          ],\n        };\n      } catch (error) {\n        if (axios.isAxiosError(error)) {\n          return {\n            content: [\n              {\n                type: 'text',\n                text: `Weather API error: ${\n                  error.response?.data.message ?? error.message\n                }`,\n              },\n            ],\n            isError: true,\n          };\n        }\n        throw error;\n      }\n    });\n  }\n\n  async run() {\n    const transport = new StdioServerTransport();\n    await this.server.connect(transport);\n    console.error('Weather MCP server running on stdio');\n  }\n}\n\nconst server = new WeatherServer();\nserver.run().catch(console.error);\n```\n\n(Remember: This is just an example–you may use different dependencies, break the implementation up into multiple files, etc.)\n\n3. The settings file may have other MCP servers already configured, so you would read it first and then add your new server to the existing `mcpServers` object.\n\nIMPORTANT: Regardless of what else you see in the MCP settings file, you must default any new MCP servers you create to disabled=false and autoApprove=[].\n\n```json\n{\n  \"mcpServers\": {\n    ...,\n    \"weather\": {\n      \"command\": \"node\",\n      \"args\": [\"/path/to/weather-server/build/index.js\"],\n      \"env\": {\n        \"OPENWEATHER_API_KEY\": \"user-provided-api-key\"\n      }\n    },\n  }\n}\n```\n\n(Note: the user may also ask you to install the MCP server to the Claude desktop app, in which case you would read then modify `~/Library/Application Support/Claude/claude_desktop_config.json` on macOS for example. (Note: If you encounter a 'not connected' error when testing a newly installed mcp server, a common cause is an incorrect build path in your MCP settings configuration. Since compiled JavaScript files are commonly output to either 'dist/' or 'build/' directories, double-check that the build path in your MCP settings matches where your files are actually being compiled. E.g. If you assumed 'build' as the folder, check tsconfig.json to see if it's using 'dist' instead.)\n\n7. Using Puppeteer MCP Server with Claude\n\nThe Puppeteer MCP server allows Claude to control a browser directly. This is useful when you want Claude to help you automate browser tasks without writing code.\n\n### Available Tools\n\n- **puppeteer_navigate**: Navigate to a URL\n  ```\n  {\n    \"url\": \"https://www.example.com\"\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **puppeteer_screenshot**: Take a screenshot\n  ```\n  {\n    \"name\": \"example_screenshot\",\n    \"width\": 1200,\n    \"height\": 800\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **puppeteer_click**: Click an element\n  ```\n  {\n    \"selector\": \"#button-id\"\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **puppeteer_fill**: Fill a form field\n  ```\n  {\n    \"selector\": \"input[name='search']\",\n    \"value\": \"search term\"\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **puppeteer_evaluate**: Execute JavaScript\n  ```\n  {\n    \"script\": \"document.title\"\n  }\n  ```\n\n### Other Available Tools\n\n- puppeteer_hover\n- puppeteer_select\n\n### Available Resources\n\n- **console://logs**: View browser console logs\n\n### Example Usage with Claude\n\nYou can ask Claude to perform browser tasks like:\n\n\"Navigate to Google and search for 'puppeteer automation'\"\n\nClaude will use the Puppeteer MCP server to execute this task.\n\n## 2. Running Puppeteer Scripts Locally\n\nFor more complex or repeatable automation tasks, you can run Puppeteer scripts directly on your computer.\n\n### Demo Script\n\nWe've created a simple demo script that shows Puppeteer's capabilities:\n\n1. Run the demo by double-clicking `run-puppeteer-demo.bat` or running it from the command line\n2. The script will:\n   - Open a browser window\n   - Navigate to Google\n   - Take a screenshot\n   - Search for \"Puppeteer automation\"\n   - Take another screenshot of the results\n   - Extract search result statistics\n   - Close the browser\n\n### Creating Your Own Scripts\n\nYou can create your own Puppeteer scripts by modifying `puppeteer-demo.js`. Here are some things you can do:\n\n- Navigate to websites\n- Fill out forms\n- Click buttons\n- Take screenshots\n- Extract data from pages\n- Automate repetitive tasks\n\n### Basic Puppeteer Code Structure\n\n```javascript\nconst puppeteer = require('puppeteer');\n\nasync function run() {\n  // Launch browser\n  const browser = await puppeteer.launch({\n    headless: false\n  });\n  \n  // Create new page\n  const page = await browser.newPage();\n  \n  // Navigate to URL\n  await page.goto('https://example.com');\n  \n  // Interact with the page\n  await page.type('#search', 'example');\n  await page.click('#submit-button');\n  \n  // Wait for navigation\n  await page.waitForSelector('#results');\n  \n  // Extract data\n  const data = await page.evaluate(() => {\n    return document.querySelector('#results').textContent;\n  });\n  \n  console.log(data);\n  \n  // Close browser\n  await browser.close();\n}\n\nrun();\n```\n\n## Resources\n\n- [Puppeteer Documentation](https://pptr.dev/)\n- [Puppeteer GitHub](https://github.com/puppeteer/puppeteer)\n"},{"type":"text","text":"<environment_details>\n# VSCode Visible Files\n../../../AppData/Roaming/Code/User/globalStorage/saoudrizwan.claude-dev/settings/cline_mcp_settings.json\n\n# VSCode Open Tabs\n.mcp.json\nrestart-filesystem-mcp.bat\ntest-mcp-filesystem.js\nupdate-mcp-settings.ps1\nmcp-filesystem-demo.js\nstart-filesystem-mcp.bat\n../../../AppData/Roaming/Code/User/globalStorage/saoudrizwan.claude-dev/settings/cline_mcp_settings.json\n\n# Current Time\n5/10/2025, 9:51:02 AM (America/Chicago, UTC-5:00)\n\n# Context Window Usage\n33,288 / 200K tokens used (17%)\n\n# Current Mode\nACT MODE\n</environment_details>"}]},{"role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"\nNow I understand what needs to be done.
